  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_df8b8fa2-20d6-4fa9-a31c-0f84cc950366'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <b></b>
</div><div></div><div>After returning home from Romania, and successfully saving her best friend Lilly, Eden Matthews must now come to terms with her future as an Immortal. She is in love with the Crowned Prince, but he is betrothed to someone else. </div><br />Her family desperately wants her to join their rebellion, but that would mean fighting against her one, true love, Kiran Kendrick. She must fight off assassins that want her dead, an Immortal rite of passage that takes her to India and a deadly disease that no one has thus far survived. Danger seems to lurk around every corner as Eden Matthews struggles to keep her true identity a secret and protect those that she loves.<br /><br />Eden must find a way to be with Kiran, or turn her back on him forever and fight to save her people. Hopeless Magic is the second installment of the Star-Crossed series.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_45442576').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_45442576').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_45442576').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2473409243" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9595023976289077471"><i>Hopeless Magic</i> is the second installment of the <i>Star-Crossed Series</i>. It definitely had it's moments where I was frustrated or rolling my eyes but in the end, I honestly really enjoyed this audio. I feel like Eden is sort of growing on me and I'm just hoping that she's realizing she's been a pawn for too long. Now is the time to take action, have revenge, and make everyone her little bitch.<br/><br/>Now the whole little "love triangle" was a bit annoying to still read in this book. I don't know about you b</span>
  <span id="freeText9595023976289077471" style="display:none"><i>Hopeless Magic</i> is the second installment of the <i>Star-Crossed Series</i>. It definitely had it's moments where I was frustrated or rolling my eyes but in the end, I honestly really enjoyed this audio. I feel like Eden is sort of growing on me and I'm just hoping that she's realizing she's been a pawn for too long. Now is the time to take action, have revenge, and make everyone her little bitch.<br /><br />Now the whole little "love triangle" was a bit annoying to still read in this book. I don't know about you but having her like a prince who was engaged to someone else was just frustrating to read about. I honestly almost stopped trying to ship her with him - I was totally down to ship her with Jericho. Maybe a rock. <br /><br />Of course her little crush doesn't go unnoticed. It's used to people's advantage without her knowledge. Then that ending, which was a bit mind blowing to read about, showed everyone's true colors. She was pissed and I loved her fighting back. Her little revenge was sweet and I'm glad that she knows who has betrayed her now. I'm just sad that her brother has been taken and her friends/family were attacked. <br /><br />Besides all of that, I did mention that I was frustrated with this book. Mostly with Eden but then again she is only 16 years old. I just wish she wasn't so focused on love or the prince. So much as going on that I was hoping they wouldn't get a happy ever after. After the audio ended, I'm actually pretty happy with the overall book. I'm pumped to dive into the third audio tomorrow and I hope it's even more entertaining.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer7874454087578608752">Okay so there were a couple things that annoyed me about this book. <br/><br/><b>Cons</b><br/><br/>-I disliked Eden so very much in this book. It's okay to make mistakes, but when you make mistakes as big as the ones she made, it makes you wonder. First off, I don't like that she's dating Kiran. It's really selfish. She is putting her family and friends at risk just so she can have a few moments with her boyfriend. There's no way I would sacrifice my family and friends for a few moments (and I do mean few seeing as their </span>
  <span id="freeText7874454087578608752" style="display:none">Okay so there were a couple things that annoyed me about this book. <br><br><b>Cons</b><br><br>-I disliked Eden so very much in this book. It's okay to make mistakes, but when you make mistakes as big as the ones she made, it makes you wonder. First off, I don't like that she's dating Kiran. It's really selfish. She is putting her family and friends at risk just so she can have a few moments with her boyfriend. There's no way I would sacrifice my family and friends for a few moments (and I do mean few seeing as their a secret and can't see each other often) with my boyfriend who just happens to be freaking ENGAGED to another girl. Next, she complains non-stop about how she's not accepted. There was a certain time where I could relate to that. To being in a new group of people and not knowing many of them, but she doesn't even make in effort. It just like hey she's a jerk. I haven't actually had a conversation with her cause I'm selfish and conceited, but I can just tell. For example when a bunch of Resistance teams from around the world come to join with her local Resistance group, there are two girls who come and introduce themselves and maybe their not that nice. So Eden then takes that time, when all the teams are there (partly to see their saviors), that she is going to run away crying, making her self the victim to every one, just because two girls were mean to her. She didn't even try to meet anybody. Made no attempts to talk to anyone. I thought that she was tougher than that, but nope. She ran crying to Kiran. So, long story short, Eden is a confused, self-centered, weak character that annoys the crap out of me!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380423587ra/843942.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>-Now this next one may be a bit of a surprise, but I also HATED Kiran. Yeah he may be hot and all but, seriously, he is a total jerk. First off, he's not willing to fight for Eden. If she is your soul mate and you love her then freaking fight for her!! Again it could be just me, but I feel like this is a problem. (And also the ending just made me hate him more.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388468804ra/7843248.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Pros</b><br><br>-I love all of Eden's friends and family. They all will always be there for her no matter how often she puts them at risk and complains. That's a real family.<br><br>-I love Eden's connection with Avalon. I love sibling chemistry that they have. It's cute.<br><br>-The plot was interesting and was one of the only things keeping me from giving up on the book. It was adventurous, exciting, and fun. I really liked the plot.<br><br>Those are really all the Pros I can thing of. I know you might be saying well there's more pros than cons so is that good? Well no, the cons are a bigger deal to me than the pros. The cons ruined the book for me. <br><br>My overall feelings for the book...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382288609i/5790470._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388468804ra/7843249.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Feelings for Eden's family...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385050372ra/7057467.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382888211ra/6259277.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="7874454087578608752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText9858163246081399976" style="display:none">Eden continues to struggle to find her place within the magical community and the Resistance. She is in love with the Prince, but not only is he betrothed to someone else, her family is also striving to end his bloodline. Rock meet hard place. Things get more interesting as the King realizes who she is and the political maneuverings begin including attempts on Eden's life.<br /><br />Things get moving in the plot in this 2nd installment of the series. Thankfully, there is enough action that it helps distract from how completely annoying Eden's character is. She is a lovesick idiot. I was constantly reminding myself that 16 year olds can be that dramatic, hormonal, and stupid! I forced myself to try to just go with it. If you compartmentalize her drama, the rest of the book is entertaining.<br /><br />If I could give it 3.5 stars, I would. It was better than the first book, and the ending gave me hope that Eden's character will mature a little in the next book. (Please!!!)</span>

<div id="review_412223346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/412223346" />
    <a title="Preeti Sharma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7399056-preeti-sharma"><img alt="Preeti Sharma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592794318p2/7399056.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/412223346?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Preeti Sharma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Preeti Sharma" href="/user/show/7399056-preeti-sharma">Preeti Sharma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Nook 2940011498428" href="/book/show/12637453-hopeless-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399056-preeti-sharma?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399056-preeti-sharma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7399056-preeti-sharma?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer412223346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9399092970351786778">I really enjoyed the Star-Crossed series, though all four books desperately need an editor. My deduction in scoring is primarily for the quality of the final product. If an author wants us to buy books, the least she should do is get her work professionally edited. I mean really, "preface" instead of "pretense", to say nothing of the numerous misplaced words throughout the draft?<br/><br/>All that aside, the story was well-told, the characters mostly believable, and the action well-paced. One major except</span>
  <span id="freeText9399092970351786778" style="display:none">I really enjoyed the Star-Crossed series, though all four books desperately need an editor. My deduction in scoring is primarily for the quality of the final product. If an author wants us to buy books, the least she should do is get her work professionally edited. I mean really, "preface" instead of "pretense", to say nothing of the numerous misplaced words throughout the draft?<br /><br />All that aside, the story was well-told, the characters mostly believable, and the action well-paced. One major exception: the king was pretty cheesy - he reminded me of a spoiled kid or a Disney villain: his "I can do whatever I want because I'm the king..." attitude grew a little tedious. If he'd had a slightly more believable justification for his craziness, this series would have been much better. I also could have done without any hint of a love triangle, but maybe I'm alone in this opinion.<br /><br />Eden makes a fun, sassy heroine, though I generally find 1st-person narration tedious, and, in the case of a teenage main character, childish. This series would have been that much better written from a 3rd-person limited perspective, perhaps focused exclusively on Eden the way Harry Potter focuses just on Harry's emotions and thoughts. I also enjoyed the descriptions of magic, though I'd have liked a little bit more on the consequences of using magic. It wasn't clear to me if the Immortals all had just an endless supply of magic always at their beck and call.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9399092970351786778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer745360563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16760100567975543843">2.5 stars. Would have been more like 4, but...<br/><br/>Well. The author certainly gives me plenty of opportunity to make criticisms. Where to begin? The grammar, spelling, punctuation, and repetitive writing style are just the beginning. (I counted about 25 instances of blushing and almost as many rolling of the eyes. I know it's teenagers we're talking about here, but come on!) I have serious issues with the character and plot development. Eden is completely unbelievable. She is probably the most uninte</span>
  <span id="freeText16760100567975543843" style="display:none">2.5 stars. Would have been more like 4, but...<br /><br />Well. The author certainly gives me plenty of opportunity to make criticisms. Where to begin? The grammar, spelling, punctuation, and repetitive writing style are just the beginning. (I counted about 25 instances of blushing and almost as many rolling of the eyes. I know it's teenagers we're talking about here, but come on!) I have serious issues with the character and plot development. Eden is completely unbelievable. She is probably the most unintelligent, dim-witted heroine I've ever encountered. She "forgets" to use her magic time after time, yet it builds up uncomfortably to the point of forced release if she doesn't? Makes no sense. She is so utterly unsure of herself that she looks to everyone else to constantly validate her. She is the last person to figure anything out - and most of the time she doesn't at all, instead being informed by another character. I know not every heroine can be smart, brave, fearless, etc, but Eden needs to have at least some redeeming qualities to make her worthy of her supposed great power and prophesied future role in the kingdom.<br /><br />*SPOILERS*<br /><br />No doubt Higginson was attempting for some big twist to the story with Kiran's betrayal. But it seemed so unrealistic! Okay, so Kiran is willing to do anything to have Eden, that's understandable. But he thinks that she's just going to go along with the sacrifice of her family and friends? “‘Oh but darling, who will give me away at our wedding?’ Eden asked, giggling and blushing.” Riiiiiiight.<br /><br />I also don't like how Higginson seems to contrive entire scenes just so that some small detail can be revealed. Eden accompanies Jericho alone, all the way to the Mexico border, just to have her meet Silas and for him to proclaim (just like the Romanian gypsy woman did) that she is the next Oracle. Nevermind that for as concerned as they've been for her safety, they were so quick to let her go on such a big trip with ONE person to protect her. It's inconsistent with the rest of the story where she has no less than 4 members of the Resistance staying in her own home to protect her at all times.<br /><br />Or when she attended Kiran's birthday party, she showed up, danced half a dance with Kiran before his father cut in, she finished the dance with him, then left?! What?? Since when would that be considered acceptable etiquette, which the Immortal society (particularly the royals) seems so concerned with? What was the point of the party scene at all? So that she could be told that Kiran's engagement was ending? Seems like that point could have been made without the unnecessary pages describing Eden preparing for a party that she would leave after 10 minutes. There are plenty of scenes where she goes somewhere only to talk to someone for a couple of minutes, then leaves.<br /><br />*END OF SPOILERS*<br /><br />Something else that bugs: where did the names of the characters come from? The author's short list of potential baby names? It's like she's trying too hard to come up with the coolest names and for me, this contributes to the absence of the characters' realism. Jericho, Avalon, Xavier, Xander, Ronan... They all have the same feel and hinders any sense of true individuality they might give the reader. <br /><br />I think the basic heart of the story is intriguing and does make me interested to find out how it all will end. But so far, I find myself rolling my eyes while reading this series more than Higginson's characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16760100567975543843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1531860271354468092">First thoughts:<br/><br/>Where do I start? Compared to the first installment in this saga this one was much more reachable; more deep. The emotions in this book was outstanding, the writing was so precise that I actually empathized with Eden. I could actually feel the emotions she was going through and boy were there a lot. The point is, "Hopeless Magic" is a book like no other and be warned, compared to the first book this one is totally different but in the best possible way.<br/><br/>Summary:<br/><br/>Lilly is finally bac</span>
  <span id="freeText1531860271354468092" style="display:none">First thoughts:<br /><br />Where do I start? Compared to the first installment in this saga this one was much more reachable; more deep. The emotions in this book was outstanding, the writing was so precise that I actually empathized with Eden. I could actually feel the emotions she was going through and boy were there a lot. The point is, "Hopeless Magic" is a book like no other and be warned, compared to the first book this one is totally different but in the best possible way.<br /><br />Summary:<br /><br />Lilly is finally back but things aren't better. Eden is the middle of two guys fighting over her and trying to keep her idenity a secret even from the man she loves the most. But soon Sabastian is introduced "Kiran's cousin" and he is there on terms that only he knows. But when he discovers that Eden was raised by human and hadn't done the traditional "Eternal Walk" she is sent to India to do just that. But the resistance and her twin brother are skeptical, thinking Luthern the king has plans of his own to take Eden. <br /><br />Eden is forced to travel, she can't not speak a word till the task is complete and she was walk through the cave to finish her task but she worries her real identity will be revealed and is scared of the outcome.<br /><br />Throughout this book Eden is put on trial after trial and not until the last few chapters does she discover the biggest trial of all.<br /><br />Last thoughts:<br /><br />You really have to appreciate this author on how she is beautiful with words and knows how to change the plot even more and make it better. I never knew this book could be better than the first but I was allowed to see sides of the characters that I hadn't been granted access to before. This is definately a more emotional read and advise if read to be far warned. What you read from this book is something you can cherish to yourself and perhaps learn a thing or two.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15426639200357941551">This book is a fantastic follow-up to Reckless Magic. I thought I would explode at the end! There is truth to the saying "There's a thin line between love and hate." The love story builds so well in this book and as a reader I was swept up in the emotions. I enjoyed how more characters appeared and you get more background on ones that were in the first book, such as Jericho. The way the male characters express themselves is beautiful. They love and protect the ones they care deeply for. Eden is </span>
  <span id="freeText15426639200357941551" style="display:none">This book is a fantastic follow-up to Reckless Magic. I thought I would explode at the end! There is truth to the saying "There's a thin line between love and hate." The love story builds so well in this book and as a reader I was swept up in the emotions. I enjoyed how more characters appeared and you get more background on ones that were in the first book, such as Jericho. The way the male characters express themselves is beautiful. They love and protect the ones they care deeply for. Eden is still behind as usual. I can't say that she is playing catch up because that implies that she knows what or where things are going and she doesn't. She is still very cute and humorous in her land of oblivion. But, to her credit it is not really her fault that people aren't upfront with her. She's been thrown into a world that she never knew existed and is sometimes expected to operate at her full potential. Amory continues to be as wise as ever and Avalon still has my heart, what a great character along with Jericho, too. I have to admit from the beginning I have been taken by Kiran he is definitely a very interesting and intriguing character that is easy to fall for. Again, a great follow-up to the first book, it was even better. I am so looking forward to the 3rd book with heighten anticipation. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4382924198300752656">Eden has not had a good couple of months... While it is great she got Lilly out of prison, barging into a court room where the king is present is not something one would call ‘under the radar’. Eden must also decide which is more important- carrying on her parent’s wishes, and joining the resistance; or be with Kiran, who also happens to be betrothed to someone else. <br/><br/>Now, the king knows that something about Eden isn’t normal, or at least not normal in the realms of immortals. Somehow, she keeps </span>
  <span id="freeText4382924198300752656" style="display:none">Eden has not had a good couple of months... While it is great she got Lilly out of prison, barging into a court room where the king is present is not something one would call ‘under the radar’. Eden must also decide which is more important- carrying on her parent’s wishes, and joining the resistance; or be with Kiran, who also happens to be betrothed to someone else. <br /><br />Now, the king knows that something about Eden isn’t normal, or at least not normal in the realms of immortals. Somehow, she keeps fighting off those that are coming after her- even with the impossible odds. The unwanted attention is not only going to make those odds worse, but life-threatening.<br /><br />My Thoughts: Holy cow, the cliff hanger at the end of this novel is insane. I finished the book and was like, “Well now I have to read the next one.” While I think that Eden’s love for Kiran isn’t exactly reciprocated, it is her first real love, and it made the story so much more realistic. I am also someone that usually likes the first book more than the second because the story is more developed- but I have to say that this is at a tie with the first book. I would recommend this book to those who liked the Collide Series by Shelly Crane, and enjoy just as much adventure as romance. <br /></span>

<div id="review_2301313590" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2301313590" />
    <a title="Katie Jones" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10980585-katie-jones"><img alt="Katie Jones" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577909156p2/10980585.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2301313590?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie Jones" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie Jones" href="/user/show/10980585-katie-jones">Katie Jones</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781477574577" href="/book/show/21032868-hopeless-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10980585-katie-jones?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi-romance">fantasy-and-sci-fi-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10980585-katie-jones?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10980585-katie-jones?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10980585-katie-jones?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2301313590&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2301313590" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12508506680059226649">HOLY SHIT.<br/><br/>I made so many notes while reading this book that I don’t possibly have the time to turn them into a more coherent review. I’m just going to tidy them up & drop them right here.<br/><br/>ON WHY I HATE KIRAN...<br/><br/>There is no way I could watch Kiran & Seraphina all over each other day in, day out & be okay with stolen moments with him. I mean he’s so not worth this effort. Have some pride Eden.<br/><br/>Why doesn’t she confront Kiran after what Jericho tells her? I question how convincing he really needs to be</span>
  <span id="freeText12508506680059226649" style="display:none">HOLY SHIT.<br /><br />I made so many notes while reading this book that I don’t possibly have the time to turn them into a more coherent review. I’m just going to tidy them up &amp; drop them right here.<br /><br />ON WHY I HATE KIRAN...<br /><br />There is no way I could watch Kiran &amp; Seraphina all over each other day in, day out &amp; be okay with stolen moments with him. I mean he’s so not worth this effort. Have some pride Eden.<br /><br />Why doesn’t she confront Kiran after what Jericho tells her? I question how convincing he really needs to be with Seraphina? I’m sure he’s supposed to make an effort but it’s also an arranged marriage. I don’t think anyone is expecting romance ffs. He even says this later in the book but then why has he been so attentive with her so far?! I JUST DON’T LIKE HIM.<br /><br />I’m not sure how to feel about the charity that Kiran shows in India. If this is truly supposed to make me like him as a character I think it’s come too late. <br /><br />The whole dance/fight was brilliant, good to see kirans true colours &amp; see Jericho stand up for Eden. But her sadness on seeing Kiran upset is so nausiating. What the F is wrong with this girl! Why does she explain her self to him. Suggesting she shouldn’t have gone to dance. What about him &amp; Seraphina? Should she stay hidden until he wants her.<br /><br />She expresses that she feels less stressed when Kiran is not around. This is not healthy.<br /><br />So Amory seems to believe Kiran &amp; I trust Amory but I just can’t like Kiran. I worry he is the intended love interest &amp; I’m just hating him more and more. Should I give him a chance? NOPE.<br /><br />ON HOW IT SUCKS TO BE EDEN...<br /><br />Sucks that she’s an outsider with both the resistance &amp; the students at school. The resistance judges her but she didn’t choose to be raised as human. On the flip side of that though she doesn’t want to join the resistance but still wants their help. YOU CAN’T HAVE IT BOTH WAYS EDEN.<br /><br />ON WHY I LOVE JERICHO...<br /><br />I am so team Jericho.<br /><br />“She is the most self-determined, amazing woman I have ever met and if I have to wait for her, I will”<br /><br />The whole Sebastian asking Eden to the dance &amp; Jericho saving the day thing is awesome!<br /><br />ON RANDOM THINGS...<br /><br />I really enjoyed the section about her journey to the caves in India &amp; the whole ritual around preparing for the Eternal Walk.<br /><br />The significance of the colours of the wind makes me all kinds of suspicious of Kiran &amp; the necklace that he gave her at the end of the last book. Then he goes &amp; reacts strangely when she changes the colour to match her dress. He seemed ‘betrayed’ what was that about?!<br /><br />ON AVALON...<br /><br />I love all the brotherly moments with Avalon; How he tries to get her with Jericho, how be blurts out about Kiran wanting sex at Thanksgiving &amp; how he doesn’t want her to go out in that dress. SO SWEET.<br /><br />ON THAT ENDING...<br /><br />When everything is revealed &amp; she finds her dark side! YES! I mean threatening Sebastian with Amelie! That shit was DARK.<br /><br />“In that moment I lost a good piece of me, a piece that stood for justice and virtue. In its place grew the darkness of hate and righteous anger. A sticky, consuming cloud of malicious vengeance spread through my veins like wild fire and clarity found me. Dangerous, vengeful clarity cleared my mind and I let out a feral battle cry, announcing that I had arrived.”<br /><br />How Kiran acts after the battle is completely batshit kookoo. I’m shocked at how obvious it is (does that mean something, I hope not) &amp; ya know it sucks for everyone but at the same time I’m like YES I WAS RIGHT. I WAS RIGHT &amp; KIRAN IS AN ASSHOLE.<br /><br />SO IN SUMMARY... this book is a roller coaster of love &amp; hate. I love this book &amp; I hate Kiren.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12508506680059226649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13316378317892234957" style="display:none">Book 30 of 2017 is Hopeless Magic from the Star-Crossed series the by Rachel Higginson.<br /><br />I read the first book from this series a month ago and enjoyed it enough to want to read the second book.<br /><br />After finishing this arduous read with a whining teenage girl and her band of merry teenage men chasing her along with the "once you have sex you are bonded for life" message, I was glad it ended. There will be no more reading from this conservative non-subtle instruction on how young women cause trouble by speaking their minds and should think carefully of who they will marry because he owns you forever.<br /><br />It. Was. Painful.<br /><br />This had to have been written by a middle aged suburban housewife who wished she had never married her boring muggle husband.<br /><br />1 spoilt Omaha teenage victim out of 5.<br /><br />Should I read this? No. The first book ends implying more lies ahead in this book but nothing does.<br />What did I learn? First books in a series should be standalone.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5995549-valentina?shelf=downloaded">downloaded</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5995549-valentina?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5995549-valentina?shelf=shape-shifters">shape-shifters</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer872423977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15767824363362018214">Holy mother-fucking hell that was <b>
  <i>freakin INTENSE</i>
</b>!! Like habanero peppers mixed with tabasco sauce intense. Just <b>wha--why--how--who--what? What the hell did I just read!!</b> Oh my god I seriously can't believe the book ended how it did. <b>
  <i>HOW COULD KIRAN DO THAT!!!!!</i>
</b> I never really liked Kiran because he's been an asshole to Eden since the first book, but I really wanted to believe the best of him and give him the benefit of the doubt despite having a bastard of a father and being a bit--or a</span>
  <span id="freeText15767824363362018214" style="display:none">Holy mother-fucking hell that was <b>
  <i>freakin INTENSE</i>
</b>!! Like habanero peppers mixed with tabasco sauce intense. Just <b>wha--why--how--who--what? What the hell did I just read!!</b> Oh my god I seriously can't believe the book ended how it did. <b>
  <i>HOW COULD KIRAN DO THAT!!!!!</i>
</b> I never really liked Kiran because he's been an asshole to Eden since the first book, but I really wanted to believe the best of him and give him the benefit of the doubt despite having a bastard of a father and being a bit--or a lot--of a prick himself. But no, he just had to prove that he was just like his father. <br /><br />I felt so so so so soooooooo terrible for Eden. She <b>absolutely</b> loved Kiran and then he goes and betrays her in the worst way possible. He totally killed their love, and I can't understand how he could think that Eden would forgive him for that. For a second I thought he was insane, <b>like literally psycho</b>, acting like everything was fine and telling Eden they had to leave like nothing had happened. He was totally unreasonable in believing Eden would keep loving him after what he did.<br /><br />This the first book I've read where two people are soul mates and absolutely love each other and one of them betrays the other in such an atrocious and horrible way. <b>
  <i>I have absolutely no idea how Eden and Kiran could possibly come back from this.</i>
</b> How do you even forgive something like that? I would find it impossible to do. I'm on the edge of my seat because I desperately want to know what happens next. Is Eden going to hook up with Jericho? Will she meet someone else? Will she forgive Kiran? Or will she stay by herself? The possibilities are endless. <br /><br />I do think she will get back with Kiran because, hello, they <b>ARE</b> soul mates, but that kind of betrayal leaves a lasting scar on a relationship; I don't see how things could ever be the same between them. I'll be excited to see how Ms Higginson handles this situation.<br /><br />On a positive note, because of what Kiran did, <b>Eden turned into a total badass</b>, and I hope she stays that way, because I'm not really a fan of wimpy, whiny, cry-baby, woe-is-me heroines. I was really getting tired of her being this helpless girl who everyone had to protect and who was always being submissive. I have high hopes that all that is over and that she is now more mature and tough.<br /><br />On another note, I love how the plot of the series is developing, with all the drama of Eden being the only hope of saving the Immortal race. I'm super excited to see how much stronger Eden's magic is going to get and how she is going to bring down the Kendrick line. If it weren't for the awesome plot full of magic, intrigue, action and mystery, I would have stopped reading a long time ago, because the romance is <b>DEFINITELY</b> not up to par. I find Kiran to be cowardly, wimpy and totally lacking as the hero, but well, that's just my opinion, you might not think so. To be honest, throughout most of this book, I actually <b>liked</b> Kiran and wanted his relationship with Eden to succeed. But now, not so much. <br /><br />There are so many more things that happened but I'm not going to reveal anything specific; you'll have to read the book and find out for yourself!!! Rarely do I give a book five stars, so believe me when I say this book is <b>AMAZING</b>.</span>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11111746-genea?shelf=books-reviewed">books-reviewed</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer462545842" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10205456119990469701">Eden was a bit more enlightened this time around although she was still being a love sick teenager. All she could see was her and Kiran, nothing else, she was blinded by her love for him. She couldn't open her eyes and see what's taking place around her, what's happening to her people. She also didn't have any respect for herself when she was okay with sneaking around with Kiran when he was betrothed to another. I had hoped she would tell him she couldn't see him anymore while he's still engaged</span>
  <span id="freeText10205456119990469701" style="display:none">Eden was a bit more enlightened this time around although she was still being a love sick teenager. All she could see was her and Kiran, nothing else, she was blinded by her love for him. She couldn't open her eyes and see what's taking place around her, what's happening to her people. She also didn't have any respect for herself when she was okay with sneaking around with Kiran when he was betrothed to another. I had hoped she would tell him she couldn't see him anymore while he's still engaged to Seraphina. She has to see Seraphina all over him everyday and him giving her presents and taking her out, and accept it. But it was okay for him to be openly jealousy and cause a scene when she's with Jericho.<br /><br />I couldn't believe it when Eden was hoping to get Lucan's approval to marry Kiran, didn't she see how bad that was. She wanted the approval of the man who's been hunting her parents for a 150 years to kill them, the man who's ancestors have being trying to kill her grandfather for centuries. How could she want to be in the same place with this man. Eden was never able to see the big picture she was living in a teenage fantasy world where the only thing important to her was her boyfriend. Yes, she is a teenager but she wasn't too young to grasp the situation her people are in and that she and her brother are their only hope.<br /><br />I always believed that Kiran loved her but I also knew he was his father's son and wondered, how much like him his he? I didn't think she was fooling Kiran and his father anymore about her relationship with Amory and Avalon. But Eden was naive enough to believe that. Avalon and Jericho gave up on convincing her about her blindness to things since she wasn't happy with them when they tried.<br /><br />Don't know who Eden will end up with in the end, Kiran or Jericho. Since Jericho appeared I've be so on on his team and then I found out he was into her, and she obviously has strong feelings for him too. I've been hoping she might choose him but Eden feels Kiran his her soul mate and nothing can happen between her and Jericho. It seemed impossible for her and Kiran and his public affections towards Seraphina didn't have to be like that since it was an arranged engagement. But I prefer Jericho mostly because I want it to be him, his love for Eden is so pure and honest.<br /><br />I just knew that something terrible would have to take place for Eden to realize the importance of the need to take action and bring down the monarchy. Of course it had to be at the expense of her family and friends. I think Avalon and Amory knew what was going to happen when Eden accepts Kiran's proposal but they didn't talk her out of it and probably decided they would sacrifice themselves for her safety. I was bawling and yelling at the pages towards the end of the book, it was such a sad ending. Can't wait to see how Eden sets out to make things right in the next book.</span>

<div id="review_622271418" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/622271418" />
    <a title="Mandy C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7400158-mandy-c"><img alt="Mandy C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434043987p2/7400158.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/622271418?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandy C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandy C" href="/user/show/7400158-mandy-c">Mandy C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer622271418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6207986892330253655">The first one in this series was interesting - just interesting enough to get you to the second one which blows the original story out of the water. After reading Hopeless Magic, I realize Reckless Magic was more of a vehicle to plod the reader through the world building and introduction of characters and relationships. It was done painlessly enough, if not somewhat juvenile. Smart move to make it a free purchase on Amazon - I became a more forgiving reader since it cost me nothing but free time</span>
  <span id="freeText6207986892330253655" style="display:none">The first one in this series was interesting - just interesting enough to get you to the second one which blows the original story out of the water. After reading Hopeless Magic, I realize Reckless Magic was more of a vehicle to plod the reader through the world building and introduction of characters and relationships. It was done painlessly enough, if not somewhat juvenile. Smart move to make it a free purchase on Amazon - I became a more forgiving reader since it cost me nothing but free time and it allowed me to get deliciously hooked on the series with Hopeless Magic.<br /><br />It starts off in the same vein as Reckless Magic. We're back at the prep school, Kiran and Eden are hiding their relationship. School dances, rivalries, Resistance meetings and the introduction of a love triangle take up the first half of the book. I had a problem buying into Kiran and Eden's relationship. While technically it was insta-love since they hated each other at first, the switch from hate to love happened with little explanation and the progression to undying, deep love happened with very little reason. For the reviewer who hated the constant use of the "smirk" for a facial expression - I am right there with you. Surely there are other ways to express Kiran's arrogance: playful sneer, sly smile, cocky grin (if the author is reading this review, just shoot me a message - there's more where that came from.) Also, whenever Kiran and Eden had any physical contact, the earth moved, magic melded, angels sang, the well of deep love rose up to the heavens...you get the idea. Sometimes subtlety goes a long way in portraying a deep longing or steadfast love. It's a very effective method and doesn't feel like emotion is being force-fed to the reader. Which is why Jericho was a much more believable match for Eden. Their quiet interactions demonstrated a growing attraction and love for one another. While I am definitely a root for the hero kind of gal, if a relationship with Jericho spares me from more of those over-the-top scenes between Kiran and Eden, I may have to switch to the underdog. The world building is amazing, though. The set up, the characters, the magic, all of it while a little stilting at first, became flawless as I continued into this second book. Almost as if I were experiencing and learning this world just as Eden did, choppy and confusing at first before fitting in. Very impressive on the part of the author. And not TOO many long run-on explanations from characters to speed up the knowing and by-passing the showing through natural story plots.<br /><br />But seriously, the last 20 pages of the book are brilliant. Excellent main character development, incredible cliff hanger, the best set up for the next in the series. Bravo, Ms. Higginson. While there are many missteps in your writing in general, you certainly know how to tell a story. Which makes forgiving the other stuff a piece of cake.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6207986892330253655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1617457606164030755">Let me first say that while reading tensions were high between Eden and I. You just can't begin to phantom how many times I wanted to ring that fictitious characters neck while calling her a straight up whore. How low must one self-esteem be to go chasing a guy that is engaged to another woman?? Read no further if you want a mystery because my rant will be filled with spoilers.   <span id="freeText1617457606164030755" style="display:none">Let me first say that while reading tensions were high between Eden and I. You just can't begin to phantom how many times I wanted to ring that fictitious characters neck while calling her a straight up whore. How low must one self-esteem be to go chasing a guy that is engaged to another woman?? Read no further if you want a mystery because my rant will be filled with spoilers. Sorry!<br /><br />Throughout the entire book I yelled at my kindle, "Kieran is using you for your magic and you my dear are nothing more than a secret whore not to be shown in public." all this while passerby's assumed I was a crazy and yelling at myself.<br />Shocking as this may come across I have to say that my favorite part in this book was when Eden finally got her head out of her own ass. <br /><br />Let me back up a bit Eden plays the role of a dirty whore with no back bone throughout buying Kieran's lines hook line and sinker. Then for some reason complains about being the other woman. Well she doesn't as much complain as she wines about having to watch Kieran's soon to be wife hanging all over him. Woman need to learn a man who say he going to leave his wife..... sorry he isn't and no man is worth having if he has to cheat on another woman to be with you. <br /><br />And while all Eden's petty whining is taking place the resistance has to step in a number of time to save her stubborn ass. For some unknown reason keeps turning her back on the Resistance and blindly follows Kieran to her totally unavoidable downfall when all the Resistance has ever done is protect her. <br /><br />I will admit I was expecting the twist in the end. All the small hints throughout added to common sense. You can't have twins without some familiar features. I just don't see how Eden didn't notice the twin thing till it was pointed out to her.... dense, need I say more! <br /><br />It sounds like I'm hating on Eden. Well because I am. Over all it was a good read. My only issue with the whole book was the author improper use of "breath" for "breathe" and it would have been that pronounced had I not been reading aloud during my many rants. <br /><br />My favorite section was the journey for the walk. Something about the woman and their vow of silence and the love they showed Eden as they had no other spoke volumes. Plus the adventure (given cooler temperatures) sounds of one I would love to take. It was a far better read than its predecessor and was definitely worth the read time in the end.<br /></span>

<div id="review_667769676" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/667769676" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7801259-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329526455p2/7801259.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/667769676?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/7801259-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer667769676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17806136942376401456">3.5 Rating. *SPOILERS AHEAD*<br/>I am glad I decided to move on to book 2 as I think it was actually a better book. There weren't as many grammar/writing issues as was the case in the first book....although definitely could use some editing to improve the read. I didn't find myself bored on this one and was pretty well paced through the book and the story flowed well. I do still find the romance piece a bit cheesy and much....its just way too overdone for my taste, but I felt more of the connection t</span>
  <span id="freeText17806136942376401456" style="display:none">3.5 Rating. *SPOILERS AHEAD*<br />I am glad I decided to move on to book 2 as I think it was actually a better book. There weren't as many grammar/writing issues as was the case in the first book....although definitely could use some editing to improve the read. I didn't find myself bored on this one and was pretty well paced through the book and the story flowed well. I do still find the romance piece a bit cheesy and much....its just way too overdone for my taste, but I felt more of the connection this time around...again just a little too overdramatic. I really liked the story and felt like there were several twists you didn't see coming. I was genuinely surprised at how it ended....while I did not expect that they would get married and be happily ever after, I did not expect the betrayal on Kirans part and the utter lack of understanding as to why she would not see his point of view and just accept and be happy with him. Seriously??? So you orchestrate a whole scenario in which you sacrifice her whole family so you can have her and preserve your bloodline and you don't think that may be an issue? On top of that, you don't seem to get why she is so enraged and are actually angry with her and tell her you are done because she is so irrational...lol....good lord. It is not like the bloodline cannot survive another way...I honestly thought based on the character building for Kiran that he would go against the family and do the "right thing"...sadly no and now I wonder how are you supposed to like him at all going forward....he just appears to be a weak, self serving jackass. I liked Eden better in this book, though she still sometimes comes off as whiney...the whole stomping her foot just seemed really immature...though I guess if she is supposed to be 16 and new to this it could be plausible. I felt she came off weak a lot and sometimes annoying....the author used the word "screeched" way too much when she was talking and if I had to read how she immediately "obeyed" Kiran on this, that and the other, I thought I was going to hurle. That being said, I really did enjoy the story and am again intrigued to see where the story goes....she defi itely knows how to end a book to interest you in the next installment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17806136942376401456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300560061" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300560061?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucie Paris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucie Paris" href="/user/show/5858545-lucie-paris">Lucie Paris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300560061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7627560934558274684">I finished my last review about "Reckless Magic" by saying: "With Eden's bad luck, barely in and out of trouble, she will lead the reader to other frenzied adventures in "Fearless Magic." I especially hope that the man of her life is really worth it...<br/>Lots of questions remain unanswered promise that I will devour with pleasure the next opus.<br/>This book is a great discovery and a stroke of heart ! Let's see the next one... " And that's exactly what happened! A second volume thrilling and intriguing</span>
  <span id="freeText7627560934558274684" style="display:none">I finished my last review about "Reckless Magic" by saying: "With Eden's bad luck, barely in and out of trouble, she will lead the reader to other frenzied adventures in "Fearless Magic." I especially hope that the man of her life is really worth it...<br />Lots of questions remain unanswered promise that I will devour with pleasure the next opus.<br />This book is a great discovery and a stroke of heart ! Let's see the next one... " And that's exactly what happened! A second volume thrilling and intriguing that I was not disappointed with...<br /><br />The reader plunges into the new immortal word of Eden filled with daily cachoteries and secret meetings. On the one hand with the monarchy and with the other actors of the revolution. Then, we find this duality once again with the birth of an ambiguous relationship between Eden and Jericho, while in parallel a deep but painful love with Kirian is established. Maybe some lengths to note in the scenes between the two lovers who are sometimes a little cutesy.<br /><br />During the adventures told with sensitivity by Rachel Higginson, Eden is struggling against her emotions, her ideals and try to find her place in a chaotic world populated by immortals.<br />So, this volume focuses on the feelings, the weight of choice, the influence of peers and the struggle to live a life according to one's wishes. While the ending is an unbearable cliffhanger deliciously orchestrated by the author to finish on a stressful note.<br /><br />An incredible end, however it has nothing unexpected in it since the clues are given along the road of the reading...<br />I can not tell you more without the risk of revealing the most exciting part of the story but this book shook my heart. I have not been able to stop myself from grasping "Hopeless Magic"!<br /><br />I continued my journey into the hectic world invented by Rachel Higginson with the greatest pleasure. And I jumped with delight for the further adventures of Eden, Avalon, Lily, Kiran and Jericho.<br /><br />Lucie<br />newbooksonmyselves.blogspot.fr</span>

<div id="review_360829838" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/360829838" />
    <a title="Mandy (I Read Indie) Anderson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3261049-mandy-i-read-indie-anderson"><img alt="Mandy (I Read Indie) Anderson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603247644p2/3261049.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/360829838?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandy (I Read Indie) Anderson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandy (I Read Indie) Anderson" href="/user/show/3261049-mandy-i-read-indie-anderson">Mandy (I Read Indie) Anderson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer360829838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17892014915290262476">**Please do not read if you have yet to read Reckless Magic!! There will possibly be spoilers for book one.**<br/><br/>Eden and Kiran are back home and keeping their relationship secret from his parents and his fiancé until he can show them that Eden is the one he wants. Only her family and friends know the truth. But each day gets harder and harder for the young couple and their forbidden love. Especially when the Prince’s cousin, Sebastian, shows up. Kiran tries to make Eden see he is here for him. Only</span>
  <span id="freeText17892014915290262476" style="display:none">**Please do not read if you have yet to read Reckless Magic!! There will possibly be spoilers for book one.**<br /><br />Eden and Kiran are back home and keeping their relationship secret from his parents and his fiancé until he can show them that Eden is the one he wants. Only her family and friends know the truth. But each day gets harder and harder for the young couple and their forbidden love. Especially when the Prince’s cousin, Sebastian, shows up. Kiran tries to make Eden see he is here for him. Only Eden believes it’s for something more…like to spy on her for the King. And when Eden starts getting attacked…it’s only a matter of time before her true identity is found out.<br /><br />Are you freakin kidding me? That was one crazy, emotionally charged ending if I have ever seen one. I am shell shocked...fambozzelled...flabbergasted! Rachel, honey dear, you took that story in a crazy way. Am I upset? Hellz no! I loved it. I am boarding that crazy train with you and riding it to the very end. Let's do this folks...jump aboard!<br /><br />Hopeless Magic was full of mystery, suspense and lots of romance. Three things I love in a book...especially the romance. But Kiran, Kiran, Kiran. What can I say about him? He had me at times wanting to pull my hair out and the next second I was secretly swooning over him. I had my doubts about him and after that ending...I am hoping the roller coaster ride is over. I am exhausted deciding if I like him or not. I do know however, that I am loving me some Jericho in Hopeless Magic...he is the one that Eden needs to get with. He is just too sweet for words.<br /><br />What starts out as kind of a slow read soon turns into a book that is anything but. Twists and turns are what this book is all about. Rachel knows what she is doing and her books are proof of that. I am addicted to her magic wielding characters and her crazy world she invented for them. So here is to Fearless Magic…I hope to read you soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17892014915290262476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/230022321?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="diana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="diana" href="/user/show/6260635-diana">diana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6260635-diana?shelf=my-favorite">my-favorite</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230022321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15106565171602953412">I cannot believe I'm done reading the second book and now I'm dying to read Fearless!<br/><br/>Hopeless Magic was really different from Reckless Magic. Although I love both books, I found Hopeless more enticing and suspenseful. It was fast-paced and has a lot more depth than Reckless. Trust me, if you love the first one, you'd love this even more.<br/><br/>This second book to the saga, introduced us to a lot of new characters. We would get to know more of the Resistance members and one member in particular would de</span>
  <span id="freeText15106565171602953412" style="display:none">I cannot believe I'm done reading the second book and now I'm dying to read Fearless!<br /><br />Hopeless Magic was really different from Reckless Magic. Although I love both books, I found Hopeless more enticing and suspenseful. It was fast-paced and has a lot more depth than Reckless. Trust me, if you love the first one, you'd love this even more.<br /><br />This second book to the saga, introduced us to a lot of new characters. We would get to know more of the Resistance members and one member in particular would definitely give the romance a whole new twist. We'd also meet Kiran's cousin (yeay, Sebastian) and the rest of his family and get face-to-face with the King. Not only that, in Hopeless Magic we'll see a lot of cheesy moments between Kiran and Eden.<br /><br />Our heroine, Eden, will be facing a lot of newfound enemies and she'll be discovering a lot more about herself and her powers. She'll come to a lot of realizations and finally be able to accept the role she has to play and the responsibility that lies ahead of her.<br /><br />Hopeless Magic is totally heartwrenching and heartbreaking. It has a lot of what-the-heck and oh-my-gosh moments. And after what happened, I really think that there's no more hope for Eden and Kiran to be together (I hope I'm wrong).<br /><br />Hopeless is an awesome book and I can't wait to read Fearless and see what happens next. Five stars for Hopeless Magic!<br /><br /><br /><i>When I said I couldn't lose you before, I meant it. I cannot live without you. You hold too much of me. I would never survive it.</i></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349090241?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiffany " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiffany " href="/user/show/783170-tiffany">Tiffany </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349090241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13530920564563121821">3.7 Which is just a tiny more stars than I gave the last one. I really like this story, and I like the characters, and I like the writing style. <br/><br/>I don't like how often it portrays the 16year old girl drinking wine all the time as something acceptable. <br/><br/>I don't like the frequency of the lusty make-out sessions. We get it, you love kissing him. Even though he sucks. Guess what? If you had kissed another (better) guy first you would have fallen "in love" with him instead. It's that feeling that she </span>
  <span id="freeText13530920564563121821" style="display:none">3.7 Which is just a tiny more stars than I gave the last one. I really like this story, and I like the characters, and I like the writing style. <br /><br />I don't like how often it portrays the 16year old girl drinking wine all the time as something acceptable. <br /><br />I don't like the frequency of the lusty make-out sessions. We get it, you love kissing him. Even though he sucks. Guess what? If you had kissed another (better) guy first you would have fallen "in love" with him instead. It's that feeling that she loves, not the character of the "man" she chose. <br /><br />I don't like how many times this mentioned sex (without anyone actually doing it) unnecessarily. Although at the same time it did encourage waiting until marriage, which makes me more forgiving.<br /><br /> And the author isn't afraid to have characters that believe in God, without making them out to be prudish losers like many people do these days. I like that. <br /><br />While Eden sometimes annoys me, she seems to be a normally likeable as far as clueless teenagers go. And what really annoys me is the way everyone is always treating her. They claim she's meant to be their hero, but treat her like a baby and shut her out all the time. <br /><br />Luckily the ending saved the day! By forcing her and everyone else to finally really make her be the hero. By making the main focus about more than obsessing about a boy who I can't stand. And by taking our passive, slightly boring, and only sometimes cool heroine and making her totally cool. At least I hope she will be in the next books. The ending is certainly promising.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13530920564563121821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nrgoC2S26p01s5LzWFM7dipFlAhjcbrUVBlY2vixRzpqx4SdI7xDBXJzbw9d0J3jJgb/qpJhfi0TY2vglddN5g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PoENSZzVfLDr7AV9jBbVAUb6gv6wPT1nrpjHtMpWqwDK/qHf29/VKKws+IGJlXOUSrnpXEEt+Z7p4vSOpzCh3A==')})
  }

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;What do you want to know, Eden? Do you want to know how upset I am that you are not going to be around anymore, that I'm going to have to disappear out of your life completely? Would you like to know how scared I am that I won't be able to protect you anymore? Maybe you want to know how terrifying it is that you are choosing to hand yourself over to the monarchy; that you are going willingly to be slaughtered and I get absolutely no say in the matter. Or maybe you wan to know how hurt I am. Is that what you want to know?&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/503072-what-do-you-want-to-know-eden-do-you-want">17 likes</a>
